What an awesome spot to grab food and do some shopping. Each spot is a bit on the expensive side but the food is really good: hearty sandwiches, loaded pizzas, lots of different breweries and tap rooms and great ice cream. You could spend a few hours here. Great for families where everyone wants to eat something different.<//text>

< Text>
Whether you're young, old, or somewhere in between, in nice weather this is the local hang out. It offers gourmet food and drinks at a variety of small restaurants and breweries, boutiques and the community market grocery store. There's coffee at one end, and ice cream at the other end, just a couple of minutes walking from one to the other.</Text>

<date>1498708626007< /date><Response>None</Response><userid>111847169733180680131<//userid><Name>Jimmy Peterson</Name>< text>
I stayed at the Barlow for two nights over this past weekend. We had a lovely time. Our accommodations were the Queen Deluxe Room. It was quiet and the room was clean. It was exactly what we were looking for. My one minor note is that there was no hand soap. We mentioned at the front desk. The lovely girl at the desk said she would speak to the cleaning staff. We arrived back and our room still did not have hand soap. We just wound up taking it off of the cleaning staff's cart. In the grand scheme of things, it was not a big deal. I would definitely stay here again. The location was perfect.<//text>

<username>Melissa Stern</username><date>1604534687447<//date>< Rating>
3< /Rating>
< text>
You get what you pay for! If you have a weak prescription and don't need them all day, every day, or if glasses are more of a fashion thing for you, then this place should be more than fine. They have a wide selection, but they're not sturdy.

If you have a strong prescription or progressive lenses and need good, solid, everyday glasses, this is not the place to go. The cover of one of the arms of my glasses came off, they had no replacement in stock, and I never received a response from their customer service line. They would literally fall off my face if I bent over. Lesson learned.

However, back before I needed glasses 24/7, I'd have been fine with them and probably wouldn't have had an issue.  Like I said, you get what you pay for!<//text>

< text>
My mother and I visited JINS to have new prescription glasses made after poor experiences with other retailers. We came in around noon on a weekday, selected frames, submitted our prescriptions, and then returned about 30-45 mins later to pick up our glasses.  The store is a short distance from Powell Street BART.

The total was around $200 for two pairs of single-vision prescription glasses with no special coatings. After dealing with tension headaches from an improperly made Rx from another retailer, I think the cost and time it took to get to this location was worth it for a properly fitting, accurate pair of glasses. They will measure your interpupillary distance (PD) during the ordering process, so don't worry if your optician didn't list on your Rx.

The customer service is phenomenal. A sales associate helped me find frames that matched my old pair. She also assisted my mother in finding frames that fit her tastes. We left very happy with our selections. The frames are stylish, very lightweight, and fit well. Minor adjustments can be made to the nose bridge on-site if need be.

There was an axis error in my glasses, but an employee noticed this, informed me, and remade my pair in about 10 minutes. I appreciate the dedication to accuracy and quality. I will definitely return to JINS for future glasses purchases.< /text>

<UserId.>108164858293013211655< /UserId.><Pics>None<//Pics>< text>
I LOVE this place! Incredibly helpful, super friendly, very knowledgeable staff! Excellent variety of high quality designer-like frame options that range from classic to on trend styles. I walked in, without an appointment, approached a sales person, explained what I needed and was seated having an eye exam within 3 minutes. The lens strength was determined, then I was taken to the women’s section of countless frame options. I tried on about 10 different style frames, narrowed it down to one, took it to the sales person assisting me, I was as given a claim ticket receipt and told my glasses would be ready within 30 minutes time. Once my eyeglasses were ready, they were custom fit to my head, over my ears for a comfortable snug fit by lightly heating and bending the arms and balanced on a flat surface to perfection. I was told should I have any issues with my new frames or lenses, if the lenses or frames were to be damaged in any way, they have a 6 month warranty and will be replaced with new frames and lenses at no additional cost to me as long as they accompany the special warranty receipt I was given with my purchase as they do not maintain my information of purchase in their data system. With the time it took for my eye exam, searching for frames and the 30 minutes it took to create my new custom reading glasses -(one lens was stronger than the other), I was in and out in 45 minutes! I was so impressed with the exemplary service and high quality eyeglasses I received (as well as a complementary fabric covered hard cover eye glass case in my choice of color + lens cleaning cloth) for a very affordable price, that I’ll be back again and again whenever I am in need of a new pair of reading glasses. I highly recommend!</text>

This is a very intimidating glasses store. Their prices are affordable - $60-$120 for full pairs, including lenses - but it has a trendy decor/vibe, so employees are very snooty and discriminatory. I've gone here a few times, and employees were fake-polite, and failed to help me find the right frames.

Though I was dressed my best, in stylish and quality clothes/accessories - the employee immediately asked me, "DO YOU HAVE A  BUDGET"?! That felt shocking and offensive. JINS is already one of the most affordable places you can get glasses in person - and she SINGLED ME OUT for asking about budget? Despite my politeness, enthusiasm for JINS, and nice clothes - she STILL stereotyped me as poor, dowdy, untrendy, "on a budget." She was also pretty condescending to me, and treated me like less than human. She selected some frames for me that were ugly and matronly - not the hip, current SF styles I would've chosen. I really needed a pair of glasses, so I just selected anything. She was pretty cold and indifferent during the checkout process, too.

<Text>Okay, THIS is the plumbing company I will use from now on. Forever.

Like you, I was also searching online for reputable plumbers in SD. Let me help you out right now -- your search is over! Don't waste another minute of your time; just call APG and rest assured you've made the right choice.

I called APG today for a slow drain in my kitchen sink. From the moment Ryan answered the phone (on the first ring), my experience with APG was fabulous. Ryan was helpful, competent, and friendly, letting me know they could come out this afternoon. I received texts throughout the morning, updating me on my estimated appt timeframe (within 30 minutes, mind you, not the "we'll be there between 8am and 8pm" stuff), and also a text letting me know when they were on the way to my place.

Garrett, the service manager, showed up right on time. He was extremely professional, friendly, careful, and informative. With some initial examination and troubleshooting, he was able to get the drain moving faster. But he did advise me that, unfortunately, the problem wouldn't be completely resolved as there was likely a larger underlying issue with a broken or fractured pipe inside the wall. When I asked him how much for the service call, he said zero -- since he wasn't able to fully eliminate the problem, there was no charge. Every other place I've ever worked with charges a flat fee just for the service call. Incredible!

It's obvious to me that APG operates on straightforward, honest, and ethical business practices and that their reputation is very important to them. <user>116052434554209974694</user>< user_name>
Michael Wiegenstein</user_name>
<time>1620254781415</time>< Rate>
5</Rate>
< text>
Again!! Another giant surprise in some place you would never expect it. With the exception of the wood chips, haha this park is pretty close to perfect. It has an old Mesquite smoker BBQ and tables for 30 or 40 people!! It has more trees than you can count and is mostly shaded because of it! It has plenty of places to sit all around the park! There are water stations all over the place and I think with everything else in this park there are probably Jacuzzi tubs getting under those wood platforms? Hahaha. There are bathrooms right next to the park and there is actually a gate so you can go out just to go into the bathroom? How handy is that the fencing again is that nice wood post fencing with the Square open fencing. There are little placards all alone dedicated to all kinds of different dogs oh, I'm sure their owners made a little donation, which is more than acceptable. All the leaves piled up outside the fence make me wonder how nice the park would be if they just let the leaves fall on the ground inside the park? Come on I've got to find something to complain about, right, it's my duty hahaha no I'm not talking about that kind of Dooty</text>

<rating>5</rating>< text>
I absolutely love this dog park!!!!!

I was going a few times a week when a group of people with larger breed dogs meet up, a meetup where someone brings coffee and food and folks donate $ to defray the costs.  Nice people and fun dogs.  I made friends with some people and my dog loved it,but there’s one man who would grab my dog by the scruff of the neck and nearly choke him out to get his dog’s ball out of my dog’s mouth (am blanking on his name but the his dog’s name is Charlie and they’re there M, W & Fri around 9:30am).

I started going to the dog park when I knew Charlie’s choking-out-other-dogs owner would not be there, and never had any problems afterwards!  In fact, I learned that many other dog owners assiduously avoid the dog park on the days the M-W-Fr folks come for the morning meet ups.  Too many dust ups and aggressive dogs then...

It’s peaceful and beautiful there (outside the brief times the meetup people take over).  Lots of trees and shade and it’s a mulch ground cover, so if it’s rainy the dog park won’t be a huge pit of mud like many CA dog parks that rarely have to consider rain and drainage concerns as drought is more common than rainstorms.

Next time I go there I will take and post photos for this review.  It’s a large complex - a County Park actually - that has campgrounds, ball fields, lots of open spaces and picnic areas, a VERY cool botanical garden, and two dog parks (a small breed fenced in park and a large breed fenced in park).  Definitely one of the coolest spots for playtime in SLO.</text>

< Text>
The plumbing at our home backed up while I was out of town. Due to the emergency nature and it happening over a holiday weekend, I called multiple plumbers to see if they could fix the issue quickly. One came out, but couldn't determine the issue. Core couldn't come out until the following Tuesday, but immediately Don noted it was a sump pump issue. < Response>
{'time': 1627066583969, 'text': 'Nobody at core is paid by piece-rate nor commission. A good plumber knows not to adjust your regulator after about a year past it’s install date because it causes the diaphragm to fail. Go get yourself a pressure gauge at Home Depot and check it once a week or so. Adjusting an old regulator is not a solution. Failure of that prv is imminent. The prices you quote of $1,000 - $1,898 reflect all options for that repair, from basic replacement to fully upgraded. Whomever adjusted that prv did so out of ignorance. Don’t make the mistake of trusting the cheap guy just because he’s cheaper. In this case the cheap guy did something he should’ve known better for, and then gave you false hope that the repair will last. It won’t. Check the pressure regularly. It’s only a matter of time now. It will cost a great deal more in the long run after failures lead to ruptures and floods.'}<//Response>

{'time': 1621382258614, 'text': 'Hello and thank you for your review. We understand how this can feel polarizing but the truth comes down to the judgement made that the condition of the valve itself can withstand the smaller repair your friend walked you through, or rather, whether the smaller repair will be a lasting repair or a short term band aid. All of this depends on the condition of the valve. Our judgement was that the condition of the valve body warranted replacement (instead of just the few parts) in order to ensure a good quality repair that will stand the test of time. The biggest factor in this is water quality and corrosion present from the leakage. We are glad you have solved the problem for now, but keep a close eye on that valve. We aren’t in the business of proposing repairs that are larger than what is most appropriate to the situation. The price you were quoted included a complete valve replacement, removing tile/wall-material and installing concealing trim to finish.'}< /Resp>

{'time': 1597360868561, 'text': 'Thank you for your determination that the water didn’t need to be turned off. You’re almost correct. You see, when a plumber works on your plumbing system, they’re liable for what happens. One of the most common hiccups on a job like this is an angle stop failure. This is a result of the extremely hard water we have in San Diego. It happens ALL the time. At the moment of failure, there’s no time to do anything but shut the water down, because of the immediate flooding that ensues. In a building like yours, that means shutting the water off to all of your neighbors for an indeterminate amount of time. So a professional knows better than to take the customers’ word for it, and instead, prepares the building for this so that when it happens it doesn’t disrupt the lives of others. < text>
I experienced low hot water pressure in my condo and called Core Plumbing.

Don came out and said he heard the water heater going when he first came in. He suspected a slab leak and recommended we call Cable, Pipe & Leak Detection.  Jose came out and found no slab leak. I was charged $230 for that.

Don came out and gave a quote of $285 to fix the water heater which apparently was the issue from the start.   In less than an hour he called and said it was fixed. I was surprised to have to pay $285 for one hour of effort. He gave me the story of how the plumbing world has changed and that a lot of plumbers only work by bids anymore.

Essentially, for about one hour of effort,  it cost me $515 to get a hot water nipple replaced which resolved the low hot water pressure.

I would seek out a plumber who  charges an hourly rate next time I have a plumbing issue.<//text>

We had a waterline connected on our refrigerator and replaced two toilets.Both jobs were completed in a timely fashion and the work was done quite well. Zach knew what he was doing and wasted no time in completing his work. The only issue we had was that when the waterline was connected and the refrigerator was pushed back against the wall is was not flush with the counters as it was before the work was done. Zach tried several things to address this issue but was only marginally successful. Update 4/4/2019-After 4 months one of the toilets that was replaced starting leaking water overall the floor in the master bathroom. I called Don at Core Plumbing on Sunday morning and was pleasantly surprised he answered the phone.
